Moreover, the identified genes have the potential for use as target candidates for genome editing to develop stress-resistant rice.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003Cdiv class=\"sec materials\" data-magellan-destination=\"sec2\" id=\"sec2\"\u003E\u003Ch2 class=\"A\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label\"\u003E2.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E Materials and methods\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cdiv class=\"sec\" data-magellan-destination=\"sec3\" id=\"sec3\"\u003E\u003Ch3 class=\"B\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label\"\u003E2.1.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E Manual curation of gene expression data from public databases\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E RNA-Seq data were collected from the National Center for Biotechnology Information Gene Expression Omnibus (NCBI GEO) (\u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov\u002Fgeo\u002F\"\u003Ehttps:\u002F\u002Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov\u002Fgeo\u002F\u003C\u002Fa\u003E) (Barrett et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r5\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Barrett, Wilhite, Ledoux, Evangelista, Kim, Tomashevsky, Marshall, Phillippy, Sherman, Holko, Yefanov, Lee, Zhang, Robertson, Serova, Davis and Soboleva\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2013\u003C\u002Fa\u003E) and European Bioinformatics Institute BioStudies (EBI BioStudies) (\u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.ebi.ac.uk\u002Fbiostudies\u002F\"\u003Ehttps:\u002F\u002Fwww.ebi.ac.uk\u002Fbiostudies\u002F\u003C\u002Fa\u003E) (Sarkans et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r51\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Sarkans, Gostev, Athar, Behrangi, Melnichuk, Ali, Minguet, Rada, Snow, Tikhonov, Brazma and McEntyre\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2018\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). In the NCBI GEO, a comprehensive search was performed using the following query: (“drought”[All Fields] OR “water deficit”[All Fields] OR “salt”[All Fields] OR “NaCl”[All Fields] OR “salinity”[All Fields]) AND “\u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E”[porgn] AND “Expression profiling by high throughput sequencing”[Filter].\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E In the EBI BioStudies, projects related to stress treatments were selected by searching with the following parameters: “Keywords: ‘RNA-Seq’ AND ‘\u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E’ AND (‘salt’ OR ‘drought’),” “Collection: ‘Array Express’.”\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E Manual curation was performed based on the search results. The manual curation process included collecting metadata from the database, such as stress treatment conditions and sample tissues, along with the raw RNA-Seq data. Based on the descriptions in the papers and database metadata, the phenotype of each cultivar was classified as either “resistant” or “susceptible” to stress. Another criterion was the presence of paired stress-treated and stress-untreated control samples in the same project. This process resulted in the creation of 105 paired datasets from 202 samples from 11 projects.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003Cdiv class=\"sec\" data-magellan-destination=\"sec4\" id=\"sec4\"\u003E\u003Ch3 class=\"B\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label\"\u003E2.2.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E Gene expression quantification\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E FASTQ-formatted files for each RNA-Seq run accession number were obtained using the prefetch and fastq-dump commands of the SRA Toolkit (v3.0.0) [\u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fgithub.com\u002Fncbi\u002Fsra-tools\"\u003Ehttps:\u002F\u002Fgithub.com\u002Fncbi\u002Fsra-tools\u003C\u002Fa\u003E]. Quality control of the raw reads was performed using Trim Galore (v0.6.7) [\u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fgithub.com\u002FFelixKrueger\u002FTrimGalore\"\u003Ehttps:\u002F\u002Fgithub.com\u002FFelixKrueger\u002FTrimGalore\u003C\u002Fa\u003E]. Transcript quantification was performed using Salmon (v1.8.0) [\u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fgithub.com\u002FCOMBINE-lab\u002Fsalmon\"\u003Ehttps:\u002F\u002Fgithub.com\u002FCOMBINE-lab\u002Fsalmon\u003C\u002Fa\u003E] (Patro et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r47\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Patro, Duggal, Love, Irizarry and Kingsford\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2017\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). We tested two reference transcriptomes from Ensembl Plants (release 56), the \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa Japonica\u003C\u002Fem\u003E IRGSP-1.0 (Oryza_sativa.IRGSP-1.0.cdna.all.fa) and the \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa Indica\u003C\u002Fem\u003E ASM465v1 (Oryza_sativa.ASM465v1.cdna.all.fa), to evaluate potential mapping biases between subspecies. The \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EJaponica\u003C\u002Fem\u003E reference (IRGSP-1.0) consistently offered higher mapping rates for most \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EIndica\u003C\u002Fem\u003E samples, likely due to more comprehensive and well-curated gene annotations. Therefore, to ensure data consistency and enable accurate gene expression comparisons, we chose to use the \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EJaponica\u003C\u002Fem\u003E reference for quantification in both \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EJaponica\u003C\u002Fem\u003E and \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EIndica\u003C\u002Fem\u003E datasets. This approach enhances comparability and unifies annotations. We also examined the assembly and gene annotation documentation for both references (\u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fplants.ensembl.org\u002FOryza_sativa\u002FInfo\u002FAnnotation\u002F#genebuild\"\u003Ehttps:\u002F\u002Fplants.ensembl.org\u002FOryza_sativa\u002FInfo\u002FAnnotation\u002F#genebuild\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fplants.ensembl.org\u002FOryza_indica\u002FInfo\u002FAnnotation\u002F#genebuild\"\u003Ehttps:\u002F\u002Fplants.ensembl.org\u002FOryza_indica\u002FInfo\u002FAnnotation\u002F#genebuild\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). The \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EJaponica\u003C\u002Fem\u003E reference (IRGSP-1.0) has been continuously updated and curated since its assembly in 2015, whereas the \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EIndica\u003C\u002Fem\u003E reference (ASM465v1) has remained largely unchanged since its assembly in 2011 and lacks recent annotations. These differences in annotation quality may explain the higher mapping rates observed when aligning \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EIndica\u003C\u002Fem\u003E samples to the \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EJaponica\u003C\u002Fem\u003E reference. Consequently, we chose the \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EJaponica\u003C\u002Fem\u003E reference to ensure comprehensive, more recent gene annotations.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E As a result, the quantitative RNA-Seq data were calculated as the TPM. To further consolidate the data for downstream analysis, we employed the tximport package (v1.26.1) to aggregate transcript-level TPM values into gene-level expression measurements. Specifically, we generated a one-to-one correspondence table linking transcript IDs (e.g., Os01t0101600–01, −02, −03) with their corresponding gene IDs (e.g., Os01g0101600) and then aggregated the TPM values of multiple isoforms belonging to the same gene by summing them.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003Cdiv class=\"sec\" data-magellan-destination=\"sec5\" id=\"sec5\"\u003E\u003Ch3 class=\"B\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label\"\u003E2.3.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E TN ratio and score calculation\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E Gene expression data from different experiments were normalized by calculating the TN ratio, which represents the ratio of gene expression between stress-treated (T) and non-treated (N) samples. If the TN ratio was higher than the threshold, the gene was considered to be upregulated; whereas if it was less than the reciprocal of the threshold, the gene was considered downregulated. Otherwise, the gene was considered unchanged. To classify the upregulated and downregulated genes, 1.5-fold, 2-fold, 5-fold, and 10-fold thresholds were evaluated, and a 2-fold threshold was adopted. Therefore, genes with a TN ratio higher than 2 were classified as upregulated, while genes with a TN ratio lower than 0.5 were classified as downregulated. The TN score of each gene was determined by subtracting the number of downregulated experiments from the number of upregulated experiments to assess changes in gene expression under stress conditions across multiple experiments. The TN ratio and TN score were computed using code that had been utilized in a previous study (Ono &amp; Bono, \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r44\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Ono and Bono\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2021\u003C\u002Fa\u003E).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003Cdiv class=\"sec\" data-magellan-destination=\"sec6\" id=\"sec6\"\u003E\u003Ch3 class=\"B\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label\"\u003E2.4.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E DESeq2 analysis\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E To complement our TN-score method, we employed DESeq2 (v1.46.0), a robust statistical tool widely recognized for identifying differentially expressed genes from RNA-seq data. Raw read counts obtained from Salmon quantification were used as input for the analysis, which compared salt-treated and untreated samples of salt-resistant cultivars. Significant expression changes were defined as at least twofold upregulation or downregulation (i.e., log\u003Csup class=\"sup\"\u003E2\u003C\u002Fsup\u003EFoldChange ≥ |1|). We applied multiple false discovery rate (FDR) thresholds – padj &lt;0.05, 0.01, 0.005, and 0.001 – to identify statistically significant changes. In subsequent analyses, we adopted the FDR threshold of padj &lt;0.05.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003Cdiv class=\"sec\" data-magellan-destination=\"sec7\" id=\"sec7\"\u003E\u003Ch3 class=\"B\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label\"\u003E2.5.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E Gene set enrichment analysis\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E Gene set enrichment analysis was performed using the web tool ShinyGO (v0.77) [\u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fbioinformatics.sdstate.edu\u002Fgo77\u002F\"\u003Ehttp:\u002F\u002Fbioinformatics.sdstate.edu\u002Fgo77\u002F\u003C\u002Fa\u003E] (Ge et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r14\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Ge, Jung and Yao\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2020\u003C\u002Fa\u003E) to analyze the DEG sets. For the \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E analysis, the species was set to “\u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa Japonica\u003C\u002Fem\u003E Group,” and the pathway database was set to “GO Biological Process.” All other parameters were set to the default settings.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003Cdiv class=\"sec\" data-magellan-destination=\"sec8\" id=\"sec8\"\u003E\u003Ch3 class=\"B\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label\"\u003E2.6.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E Visualization\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E A web-based Venn diagram tool [\u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fbioinformatics.psb.ugent.be\u002Fwebtools\u002FVenn\u002F\"\u003Ehttps:\u002F\u002Fbioinformatics.psb.ugent.be\u002Fwebtools\u002FVenn\u002F\u003C\u002Fa\u003E] and the UpSet plot tool [\u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fasntech.shinyapps.io\u002Fintervene\u002F\"\u003Ehttps:\u002F\u002Fasntech.shinyapps.io\u002Fintervene\u002F\u003C\u002Fa\u003E] (Khan &amp; Mathelier, \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r30\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Khan and Mathelier\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2017\u003C\u002Fa\u003E) were used to search for and visualize overlapping genes.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003Cdiv class=\"sec\" data-magellan-destination=\"sec9\" id=\"sec9\"\u003E\u003Ch3 class=\"B\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label\"\u003E2.7.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E Functional annotation of \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E genes\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E To functionally annotate the \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E genes, we retrieved the “Gene ID,” “Gene name,” and “Gene description” for each gene from the Ensembl Plants (release 56, \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa Japonica\u003C\u002Fem\u003E Group genes (IRGSP-1.0)). We then identified the putative orthologs of these genes in \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EA. thaliana\u003C\u002Fem\u003E by performing a BLASTP (v2.12.0) search using the \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E protein sequences (\u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOryza_sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E.IRGSP-1.0.pep.all.fa.gz) as queries against the \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EA.thaliana\u003C\u002Fem\u003E protein database obtained from Ensembl Plants (release 56, \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EArabidopsis_thaliana\u003C\u002Fem\u003E.TAIR10.pep.all.fa.gz). The BLASTP search was conducted with an \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EE\u003C\u002Fem\u003E-value cutoff of 1e−10. For each \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E gene, the top hit in the \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EA. thaliana\u003C\u002Fem\u003E protein database was considered the putative ortholog. The corresponding “Gene ID,” “Gene name,” and “Gene description” for the \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EA. thaliana\u003C\u002Fem\u003E orthologs were obtained from the Ensembl Plants (release 56, \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EA. thaliana\u003C\u002Fem\u003E genes (TAIR10)).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003Cdiv class=\"sec results\" data-magellan-destination=\"sec10\" id=\"sec10\"\u003E\u003Ch2 class=\"A\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label\"\u003E3.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E Results\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cdiv class=\"sec\" data-magellan-destination=\"sec11\" id=\"sec11\"\u003E\u003Ch3 class=\"B\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label\"\u003E3.1.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E Overview of this study\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E Initially, we present an overview of the entire study. Through comprehensive data analysis, this research aimed to achieve two primary objectives:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Col class=\"list number nomark\"\u003E\n\u003Cli class=\"list-item\"\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label\"\u003E(1)\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E Identification of genes suggested to contribute to stress tolerance phenotypes in \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa.\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli class=\"list-item\"\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label\"\u003E(2)\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E Identification of genes implicated by the data to be involved in common stress response mechanisms across plant species, specifically in \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E and \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EA. thaliana.\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fol\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E This study consisted of six steps as shown in \u003Ca class=\"xref fig\" href=\"#fig2\"\u003EFigure 1\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Csection\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"fig-ada\" data-magellan-destination=\"fig2\" id=\"fig2\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"caption\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label\"\u003EFigure 1.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003EOverview of the six steps of this study. Step 1: RNA-Seq data for \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOryza sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E were retrieved from public databases (National Center for Biotechnology Information Gene Expression Omnibus (NCBI GEO) and European Bioinformatics Institute BioStudies (EBI BioStudies). Step 2: Samples were categorized according to stress type (salt\u002Fdrought) and phenotype (resistant\u002Fsusceptible). Differentially expressed genes (DEGs) were identified using the TN-score method. Step 3: Enrichment analysis was performed on the DEGs for each phenotype and stress condition to evaluate the validity of the analysis. Step 4: Genes involved in the phenotypic differences between \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E cultivars were selected under drought and salt stress conditions. Step 5: Common genes among different stress conditions were selected. Step 6: Genes involved in stress response mechanisms conserved across different plant species were selected.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\n\u003Cdiv class=\"figure-thumb\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"data:image\u002Fgif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAMLCwgAAACH5BAAAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAICRAEAOw==\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fstatic.cambridge.org\u002Fbinary\u002Fversion\u002Fid\u002Furn:cambridge.org:id:binary:20250905043713754-0114:S2632882825100209:S2632882825100209_fig1.png?pub-status=live\" class=\"aop-lazy-load-image\" width=\"2050\" height=\"2346\" data-original-image=\"\u002Fbinary\u002Fversion\u002Fid\u002Furn:cambridge.org:id:binary:20250905043713754-0114:S2632882825100209:S2632882825100209_fig1.png\" data-zoomable=\"true\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fsection\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003Cdiv class=\"sec\" data-magellan-destination=\"sec12\" id=\"sec12\"\u003E\u003Ch3 class=\"B\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label\"\u003E3.2.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E Retrieval and curation of RNA-Seq data from public databases\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E RNA-Seq data were retrieved from the National Center for Biotechnology Information Gene Expression Omnibus (NCBI GEO) and European Bioinformatics Institute BioStudies (EBI BioStudies) public databases. Compared with microarray data, RNA-Seq data were primarily derived from the Illumina platform, making them more suitable for comparative analyses of studies from different research groups. Therefore, only RNA-Seq data were used in this study, while microarray data were excluded. In this study, based on the description in the papers and metadata of databases, the phenotype of cultivars reported to present strong resistance was defined as “resistant” and the cultivars reported to present relatively weak resistance were defined as “susceptible.” A total of 202 samples were collected from the 11 projects, resulting in 105 paired datasets of stress-treated and untreated control samples. Because of manual curation, the collected data were divided into four categories based on the stress type and phenotype: (1) salt-resistant, (2) salt-susceptible, (3) drought-resistant, and (4) drought-susceptible. The number of paired datasets for each category was as follows: 24 for salt-resistant, 36 for salt-susceptible, 31 for drought-resistant, and 14 for drought-susceptible. To systematically organize the data used in the analysis, a table including the stress type, phenotype, subspecies, research project ID, and experimental pair number was prepared for each rice variety (Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003ETable S1\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). When the number of collected sample pairs was compared among the tissues, it was revealed that samples derived from “leaf” contained the most data (Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003EFigure S1\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). Details on all other metadata are presented in Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003ETable S2\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003Cdiv class=\"sec\" data-magellan-destination=\"sec13\" id=\"sec13\"\u003E\u003Ch3 class=\"B\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label\"\u003E3.3.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E Analysis of collected data and selection of differentially expressed genes in \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E The collected samples were subjected to quality control and expression quantification using Salmon(Patro et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r47\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Patro, Duggal, Love, Irizarry and Kingsford\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2017\u003C\u002Fa\u003E), which calculated the transcripts per million (TPM) values for each gene in each sample (Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003ETable S3\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). Stress-treated and non-treated samples were paired for each gene, and the expression ratios (TN ratios) and TN scores were calculated. The TN ratio was calculated as follows:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cdiv data-mathjax-status=\"texmath alt-graphic\" class=\"disp-formula\" data-magellan-destination=\"eqn1\" id=\"eqn1\"\u003E\n\u003Cspan class=\"alternatives\"\u003E\n\u003Cspan class=\"mathjax-tex-wrapper\" data-mathjax-type=\"texmath\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"tex-math mathjax-tex-math mathjax-on\"\u003E\n$$\\begin{align*}&amp;\\mathrm{TN}\\;\\mathrm{ratio}=\\left(\\mathrm{stress}\\hbox{-} \\mathrm{treated}\\;\\mathrm{TPM}+1\\right)\u002F\\\\&amp;\\quad\\left(\\mathrm{non}\\hbox{-} \\mathrm{treated}\\;\\mathrm{TPM}+1\\right).\\end{align*}$$\n\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\n\u003Cimg src=\"data:image\u002Fgif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAMLCwgAAACH5BAAAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAICRAEAOw==\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fstatic.cambridge.org\u002Fbinary\u002Fversion\u002Fid\u002Furn:cambridge.org:id:binary:20250905043713754-0114:S2632882825100209:S2632882825100209_eqnu1.png?pub-status=live\" class=\"aop-lazy-load-image mathjax-alternative mathjax-alt-graphic mathjax-off\" width=\"307\" height=\"49\" data-original-image=\"\u002Fbinary\u002Fversion\u002Fid\u002Furn:cambridge.org:id:binary:20250905043713754-0114:S2632882825100209:S2632882825100209_eqnu1.png\" data-zoomable=\"false\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E If the TN ratio was higher than the threshold, the gene was considered upregulated; whereas if it was lower than the reciprocal of the threshold, it was considered downregulated. Otherwise, it was considered unchanged. To classify the upregulated and downregulated genes, we evaluated 1.5-fold, 2-fold, 5-fold, and 10-fold thresholds and finally chose the 2-fold threshold. Therefore, genes with a TN ratio higher than 2 were classified as upregulated, while genes with a TN ratio lower than 0.5 were classified as downregulated. The TN score of each gene was determined by subtracting the number of downregulated experiments from the number of upregulated experiments to assess changes in gene expression under stress conditions across the entire experiment.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Csection\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"table-wrap-ada\" data-magellan-destination=\"tab1\" id=\"tab1\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"caption\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label\"\u003ETable 1\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003EDistribution of DEG numbers and TN2 scores in \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOryza sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E under different stress conditions and phenotypes based on the meta-analysis\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\n\n\n\u003Cdiv class=\"figure-thumb\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"data:image\u002Fgif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAMLCwgAAACH5BAAAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAICRAEAOw==\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fstatic.cambridge.org\u002Fbinary\u002Fversion\u002Fid\u002Furn:cambridge.org:id:binary:20250905043713754-0114:S2632882825100209:S2632882825100209_tab1.png?pub-status=live\" class=\"aop-lazy-load-image\" width=\"1012\" height=\"261\" data-original-image=\"\u002Fbinary\u002Fversion\u002Fid\u002Furn:cambridge.org:id:binary:20250905043713754-0114:S2632882825100209:S2632882825100209_tab1.png\" data-zoomable=\"true\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fsection\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E The collected samples were classified into the four aforementioned categories based on the phenotype and type of stress treatment, and the TN scores for each category were calculated. After considering multiple expression ratio thresholds, we adopted a 2-fold threshold (TN2). This threshold was slightly lower to provide a comprehensive analysis. More severe scores for the 5-fold (TN5) and 10-fold (TN10) thresholds were also calculated and are listed in the \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003ESupplementary Table\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. The TN ratios and TN scores for all the genes are available online (Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003ETables S4\u003C\u002Fa\u003E and \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003ES5\u003C\u002Fa\u003E).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E Additionally, the distribution of TN scores for the genes was visualized using scatter plots (Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003EFigure S2\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). Focusing on points where scores changed significantly on the scatter plot, the top and bottom genes based on TN2 scores were selected as differentially expressed genes (DEGs). This accounted for the top or bottom 1% of all reference genes. Abrupt score changes indicated that the expression of these genes was remarkably variable in the dataset used in this study. The number of identified genes and range of TN2 scores are summarized in \u003Ca class=\"xref table\" href=\"#tab1\"\u003ETable 1\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Lists of the upregulated and downregulated genes are available online (Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003ETables S6\u003C\u002Fa\u003E and \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003ES7\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, respectively). For the DEGs identified in rice, the corresponding orthologs in \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EArabidopsis thaliana\u003C\u002Fem\u003E were determined using sequence similarity searches with BLASTP. The list of these genes is available online (Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003ETable S8\u003C\u002Fa\u003E).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003Cdiv class=\"sec\" data-magellan-destination=\"sec14\" id=\"sec14\"\u003E\u003Ch3 class=\"B\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label\"\u003E3.4.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E Comparison of DEGs Identified by TN2 and DESeq2\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E Similarly, we identified differentially expressed genes (DEGs) using DESeq2 on salt-resistant rice samples comprising 24 salt-treated and 24 untreated specimens. In our DESeq2 analysis, genes were considered differentially expressed if their expression changed by at least a twofold ratio (log\u003Csup class=\"sup\"\u003E2\u003C\u002Fsup\u003E fold change ≥1) and met specific false discovery rate (FDR) thresholds. We tested four FDR values – 0.05, 0.01, 0.005, and 0.001 – and at FDR &lt; 0.05, DESeq2 identified 82 upregulated genes. To evaluate the concordance between DESeq2 and the TN-score method, we compared the DEGs from DESeq2 with the 397 genes selected via the TN-score approach (Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003ETable S9\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). Notably, 54 of the 82 upregulated genes (approximately 65.8%) identified by DESeq2 overlapped with the TN-score selection. This overlap substantiates the efficacy of the TN-score methodology by demonstrating its ability to capture a substantial proportion of genes exhibiting statistically significant expression changes while also identifying many additional genes not detected by DESeq2.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E To address the biological significance of genes identified by the TN-score method but missed by DESeq2, Gene Ontology (GO) enrichment analysis was performed on DEG sets. These included those commonly identified by both methods and those identified by either method alone (Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003ETable S10\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003EFigure S3\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). The results revealed that the gene set uniquely identified by the TN-score method (343 genes) showed significant enrichment in multiple GO terms related to important biological functions, such as the stress response (e.g., Cold acclimation, Response to cold, Response to water deprivation and Response to abscisic acid), compared to the gene set uniquely identified by DESeq2 (28 genes). This suggests that the TN-score method captures a biologically meaningful set of genes overlooked by DESeq2. Notably, the TN-score-specific DEGs included four Dehydrin proteins, \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003ERAB16A\u003C\u002Fem\u003E (\u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOs11g0454300\u003C\u002Fem\u003E), \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003ERAB16B\u003C\u002Fem\u003E (\u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOs11g0454200\u003C\u002Fem\u003E), \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003ERAB16C\u003C\u002Fem\u003E (\u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOs11g0454000\u003C\u002Fem\u003E), and \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003ERAB16D\u003C\u002Fem\u003E (\u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOs11g0453900\u003C\u002Fem\u003E), which were classified under all the aforementioned stress-related GO terms. Although the precise molecular functions of Dehydrins are still not fully understood, these Group II Late Embryogenesis Abundant (LEA) proteins are characterized by high hydrophilicity (Liu et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r35\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Liu, Song, Li, Yang and Li\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2017\u003C\u002Fa\u003E; Sun et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r57\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Sun, Li, Chen, Zhang, Zhang, Sun and Wang\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2021\u003C\u002Fa\u003E; Szlachtowska &amp; Rurek, \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r58\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Szlachtowska and Rurek\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2023\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). Their expression is induced in response to abiotic stresses such as salt, drought and low temperature, and they are believed to contribute to plant stress tolerance through mechanisms including the stabilization of biological membranes, protection of enzyme activity, or binding to metal ions. Plants accumulate highly hydrophilic dehydrins, which enable them to retain water and reduce cellular dehydration and damage caused by osmotic pressure, especially under conditions that disrupt intracellular water homeostasis, such as high salinity. Furthermore, the TN-score-specific DEGs also contained other genes belonging to families involved in salt and drought stress responses, such as \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOsPP2C50\u003C\u002Fem\u003E (\u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOs05g0537400\u003C\u002Fem\u003E), \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOsABA45\u003C\u002Fem\u003E (\u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOs12g0478200\u003C\u002Fem\u003E), \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOsPSY\u003C\u002Fem\u003E (\u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOs09g0555500\u003C\u002Fem\u003E), \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOsPP2C30\u003C\u002Fem\u003E (\u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOs03g0268600\u003C\u002Fem\u003E) and \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003ELEA17\u003C\u002Fem\u003E (\u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOs03g0322900\u003C\u002Fem\u003E). These uniquely identified genes provide the evidence for the efficacy of the TN-score method in identifying biologically important stress-responsive genes that have not been detected by DESeq2 approaches.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E Overall, the complementary use of the TN-score method alongside conventional statistical approaches offers an effective strategy for comprehensive gene expression analysis in meta-studies. The read count data used for the DESeq2 analysis and the corresponding DEGs are listed in Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003ETable S9\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003Cdiv class=\"sec\" data-magellan-destination=\"sec15\" id=\"sec15\"\u003E\u003Ch3 class=\"B\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label\"\u003E3.5.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E Enrichment analysis to evaluate the characteristics of DEGs\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E To evaluate the characteristics of the identified DEGs, we performed enrichment analyses of individual DEG groups using ShinyGO. The results are shown in Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003EFigure S4\u003C\u002Fa\u003E and Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003ETable S11\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. The top two GO terms for each DEG are listed in Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003ETable S12\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E Enrichment analysis revealed distinct patterns of gene regulation under different stress conditions and phenotypes. These results suggest that diverse stress response mechanisms may exist depending on the type of stress and phenotypic traits.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E Furthermore, we focused on DEGs that showed similar expression patterns (upregulation or downregulation) across different phenotypes and stress conditions and considered them as a single group. We performed enrichment analyses for two types of combined DEGs. The first group consisted of all genes whose expression was upregulated under at least one condition (Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003EFigure S5a\u003C\u002Fa\u003E), and the second group consisted of all genes whose expression was downregulated under at least one condition (Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003EFigure S5b\u003C\u002Fa\u003E).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E For upregulated DEGs (Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003EFigure S5a\u003C\u002Fa\u003E), the most significantly enriched terms were “diterpenoid metabolic processes” and “water deprivation.” Other enriched terms included responses to various abiotic stressors, such as heat and salt stress, and hormone responses, especially abscisic acid (ABA). These results support the validity of the selection of DEGs responsive to salt and drought stress by the meta-analysis.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E For the downregulated genes (Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003EFigure S5b\u003C\u002Fa\u003E), the analysis revealed a different set of enriched terms. The most significantly enriched terms were related to nitrogen metabolism, including “nitrate metabolic processes,” “nitrate assimilation,” and “reactive nitrogen species metabolic processes.” Interestingly, several terms involved in oxidative stress response and detoxification were also significantly enriched, such as “hydrogen peroxide catabolic process” and “reactive oxygen species metabolic process.” Additionally, photosynthesis-related processes and transmembrane transport were among the enriched pathways for downregulated genes. Detailed results of the enrichment analysis for individual DEGs and all combined DEGs are provided in Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003ETable S9\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003Cdiv class=\"sec\" data-magellan-destination=\"sec16\" id=\"sec16\"\u003E\u003Ch3 class=\"B\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label\"\u003E3.6.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E Selection of genes involved in phenotypic differences between \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E cultivars under drought and salt stress conditions\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E We compared the DEGs between the stress-resistant and stress-susceptible phenotypes for both salt and drought stress to identify genes specific to each condition (Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003EFigure S6\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). The numbers of common and unique genes in each group are summarized in Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003ETable S13\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E We conducted an enrichment analysis of these individual gene sets, and the results are shown in Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003EFigure S6\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. However, as no hits were found in gene set (j), only those for the “All available gene sets” setting were used. The top GO terms for each DEG are summarized in Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003ETable S14\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E Interestingly, the enrichment analysis showed that the most significantly enriched term for both the upregulated genes in the salt susceptible and salt resistant groups, as well as the drought susceptible and drought resistant groups, was “GO:0009631 Cold acclimation.” This suggests that the importance of stress mechanisms of cold acclimation may be similar to that of both salinity and drought stress, regardless of the \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E phenotype.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E In addition, in Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003EFigure S6a\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, the most significantly enriched term in the enrichment analysis of the upregulated combined DEGs was “diterpenoid metabolic processes.” In contrast, the most significantly enriched term in the genes specifically downregulated in the drought-resistant phenotype was “diterpenoid biosynthesis (KEGG: osa00904).” This suggests that the pathways involving diterpenoids may regulate stress responses by upregulating or downregulating the expression of related genes. All gene lists, Venn diagrams visualizing overlapping genes, and enrichment results are shown in \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003ESupplementary Tables\u003C\u002Fa\u003E (Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003ETables S15\u003C\u002Fa\u003E and \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003ES16\u003C\u002Fa\u003E).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003Cdiv class=\"sec\" data-magellan-destination=\"sec17\" id=\"sec17\"\u003E\u003Ch3 class=\"B\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label\"\u003E3.7.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E Selection of genes common among different stress conditions\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E The overlap of genes that were commonly upregulated or downregulated across the four categories based on the two stress conditions and two phenotypes each was visualized using UpSet plots (\u003Ca class=\"xref fig\" href=\"#fig3\"\u003EFigure 2\u003C\u002Fa\u003E).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Csection\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"fig-ada\" data-magellan-destination=\"fig3\" id=\"fig3\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"caption\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label\"\u003EFigure 2.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003EUpSet plots showing the overlap and specificity of DEGs in \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOryza sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E under various stress conditions and phenotypes. UpSet plots illustrating the overlap of commonly or specifically regulated genes across the four categories combining salt and drought stress conditions with resistant and susceptible phenotypes. (a) Upregulated genes; (b) downregulated genes.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\n\u003Cdiv class=\"figure-thumb\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"data:image\u002Fgif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAMLCwgAAACH5BAAAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAICRAEAOw==\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fstatic.cambridge.org\u002Fbinary\u002Fversion\u002Fid\u002Furn:cambridge.org:id:binary:20250905043713754-0114:S2632882825100209:S2632882825100209_fig2.png?pub-status=live\" class=\"aop-lazy-load-image\" width=\"1921\" height=\"2500\" data-original-image=\"\u002Fbinary\u002Fversion\u002Fid\u002Furn:cambridge.org:id:binary:20250905043713754-0114:S2632882825100209:S2632882825100209_fig2.png\" data-zoomable=\"true\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fsection\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E All overlapping genes are listed in Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003ETable 17\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. The number of genes whose expression specifically increased or decreased in each phenotype under both stress conditions is summarized in Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003ETable S18\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E Among these genes, those whose expression was upregulated in the resistant and susceptible varieties are summarized in \u003Ca class=\"xref table\" href=\"#tab2\"\u003ETable 2\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Csection\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"table-wrap-ada\" data-magellan-destination=\"tab2\" id=\"tab2\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"caption\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label\"\u003ETable 2\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003EList of \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOryza sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E genes that were specifically upregulated in the resistant or susceptible phenotype under both salt and drought stress conditions\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\n\n\n\u003Cdiv class=\"figure-thumb\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"data:image\u002Fgif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAMLCwgAAACH5BAAAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAICRAEAOw==\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fstatic.cambridge.org\u002Fbinary\u002Fversion\u002Fid\u002Furn:cambridge.org:id:binary:20250905043713754-0114:S2632882825100209:S2632882825100209_tab2.png?pub-status=live\" class=\"aop-lazy-load-image\" width=\"1056\" height=\"777\" data-original-image=\"\u002Fbinary\u002Fversion\u002Fid\u002Furn:cambridge.org:id:binary:20250905043713754-0114:S2632882825100209:S2632882825100209_tab2.png\" data-zoomable=\"true\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fsection\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E In total, 10 genes were consistently upregulated in the resistant phenotype under both stress conditions. These included genes involved in various cellular processes, such as transcription regulation (\u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOshox25\u003C\u002Fem\u003E and \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EPHR3\u003C\u002Fem\u003E), secondary metabolism (\u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOsOSC4\u003C\u002Fem\u003E and \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOsPSY\u003C\u002Fem\u003E), and peroxidase (\u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003Eprx130\u003C\u002Fem\u003E).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E In contrast, 12 genes were consistently upregulated in the susceptible phenotype under both salt and drought stress conditions. These genes have different functional profiles, including a bHLH transcription factor (\u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOsbHLH035\u003C\u002Fem\u003E), glycine-rich cell wall structural protein (\u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EGRP\u003C\u002Fem\u003E), hypoxia-induced gene (\u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EHIGD2\u003C\u002Fem\u003E), and enzymes involved in various metabolic processes (\u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003ERRJ1\u003C\u002Fem\u003E and \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EC10923\u003C\u002Fem\u003E).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003Cdiv class=\"sec\" data-magellan-destination=\"sec18\" id=\"sec18\"\u003E\u003Ch3 class=\"B\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label\"\u003E3.8.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E Selection of genes involved in stress response mechanisms conserved across different plant species\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E In a previous study, we performed a meta-analysis of \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EA. thaliana\u003C\u002Fem\u003E under ABA, salt, and dehydration conditions and identified genes that were upregulated or downregulated under each condition (Shintani et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r53\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Shintani, Tamura and Bono\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2024\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). Here, we used \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EA. thaliana\u003C\u002Fem\u003E orthologous genes corresponding to the \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E genes identified in this study to determine whether any genes shared commonality. The overlap in expression of commonly regulated genes was visualized using UpSet plots (Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003EFigure S7\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). Satisfying the above criteria, 11 genes were upregulated (At_ABA_up, At_Dehydration_up, At_Salt_up, Os_Drought_Resistant_up, Os_Drought_Susceptible_up, Os_Salt_Resistant_up, and Os_Salt_ Susceptible_up) and 1 gene was downregulated (At_ABA_down, At_Dehydration_down, At_Salt_down, Os_Drought_Resistant_ down, Os_Drought_Susceptible_down, Os_Salt_Resistant_down, and Os_Salt_Susceptible_down) under salt and drought conditions (\u003Ca class=\"xref table\" href=\"#tab3\"\u003ETable 3\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). These genes may be involved in the stress response mechanisms that are common across different plant species.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Csection\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"table-wrap-ada\" data-magellan-destination=\"tab3\" id=\"tab3\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"caption\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label\"\u003ETable 3\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003EComparison of ABA, salt, and drought stress-responsive genes conserved in rice and \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EArabidopsis\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\n\n\n\u003Cdiv class=\"figure-thumb\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"data:image\u002Fgif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAMLCwgAAACH5BAAAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAICRAEAOw==\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fstatic.cambridge.org\u002Fbinary\u002Fversion\u002Fid\u002Furn:cambridge.org:id:binary:20250905043713754-0114:S2632882825100209:S2632882825100209_tab3.png?pub-status=live\" class=\"aop-lazy-load-image\" width=\"1071\" height=\"878\" data-original-image=\"\u002Fbinary\u002Fversion\u002Fid\u002Furn:cambridge.org:id:binary:20250905043713754-0114:S2632882825100209:S2632882825100209_tab3.png\" data-zoomable=\"true\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fsection\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E For the \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E genes in the ‘resistant’ phenotype category used in this study, six genes were upregulated (At_ABA_up, At_Dehydration_up, At_Salt_up, Os_Drought_Resistant_up, and Os_Salt_Resistant_up) and one gene was downregulated (At_ABA_down, At_Dehydration_down, At_Salt_down, Os_ Drought_Resistant_down, and Os_Salt_Resistant_down) was downregulated under salt and drought conditions (\u003Ca class=\"xref table\" href=\"#tab3\"\u003ETable 3\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). These genes may be involved in stress responses that are common across plant species, particularly in mechanisms important for stress tolerance.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E The list of \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E gene IDs identified in this study was converted to \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EA. thaliana\u003C\u002Fem\u003E IDs and compared with previous studies. All gene lists are available online (Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003ETable S19\u003C\u002Fa\u003E).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003Cdiv class=\"sec discussion\" data-magellan-destination=\"sec19\" id=\"sec19\"\u003E\u003Ch2 class=\"A\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label\"\u003E4.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E Discussion\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E This study aimed to identify novel genes and potential pathways involved in drought and salt stress responses in \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E using a meta-analysis of publicly available RNA-Seq data. By integrating datasets from multiple studies covering different \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E cultivars and stress conditions, we aimed to reveal robust and consistent gene expression patterns associated with stress resistance or susceptibility. Analysis of the tissue types of the collected samples revealed that while salt and drought stress are expected to have significant effects on the roots, the majority of the affected samples in this study consisted of “leaf” and “shoot” tissues, with a limited number of “root-“specific samples. Although this study focused on phenotypes and stress types rather than tissue specificity, tissue-specific analyses will likely become possible in the future as the amount of publicly available RNA-Seq data increases.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E This study focused on several \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E cultivars that exhibited different phenotypic responses to salt and drought stress. The phenotypic classifications of “resistant” and “susceptible” used in this study are based solely on existing research reports and may not fully capture the nuanced stress tolerance levels of each cultivar. In addition, differences in stress treatment methods among the studies should be considered.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E To minimize the impact of these differences and provide a robust comparative analysis of multiple datasets, we adopted the following approach. First, we directly compared the gene expression ratios between stressed and control samples in the same study. Subsequently, we calculated the TN score, which facilitated integration and comparative analysis of the data across multiple studies.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E Based on the TN score, DEGs were identified for each dataset and categorized by stress type and phenotype. Enrichment analysis of each DEG set revealed the distinct and characteristic terms associated with each DEG group. Furthermore, we performed an enrichment analysis of genes that were upregulated or downregulated, irrespective of the phenotypic classification or stress type. The most significantly enriched term for upregulated genes was “diterpenoid metabolic process,” with 13 genes included in this category (Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003EFigure S5 (b)\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). Diterpenoid phytoalexins have been shown to be potentially involved in the resistance of cereal plants to environmental stresses, such as drought (Murphy &amp; Zerbe, \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r43\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Murphy and Zerbe\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2020\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). The genes are listed in Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003ETable S20\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E These genes included those whose functions in stress mechanisms have been elucidated in previous studies. \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOsCPS4\u003C\u002Fem\u003E encodes a key enzyme that contributes to the biosynthesis of labdane-related diterpenoid (LRD) phytoalexins in \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E. Mutant analysis showed that the loss of function of \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOsCPS4\u003C\u002Fem\u003E significantly increased sensitivity to drought stress, suggesting that LRD biosynthesis involving \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOsCPS4\u003C\u002Fem\u003E contributes to the regulation of stomatal closure, independent of the ABA pathway (Zhang et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r68\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Zhang, Li, Xu, Hoffmann, Zhang, Liu, Zhang, Yang, Li and Peters\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2021\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). The genes with unknown functions listed in this study may include those that contribute to the stress response through their involvement in LRD metabolism. Interestingly, in addition to the upregulated DEGs, the term enriched in genes specifically downregulated in the drought stress susceptible samples was “diterpenoid biosynthesis (KEGG: osa00904)” (Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003EFigure S6 (d)\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003ETable S20\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). This contrasting expression pattern suggests a complex regulatory mechanism in the diterpenoid pathway. In other words, the genes in this pathway may show diverse expression patterns depending on the type of stress, plant phenotype, and cultivar.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E We also focused on a group of genes whose expression was upregulated in both the resistant and susceptible cultivars under the two stresses. Some of the genes commonly upregulated under salt and drought stress in the resistant phenotype included \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOsPSY3\u003C\u002Fem\u003E (\u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOs09g0555500\u003C\u002Fem\u003E). \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EPSY\u003C\u002Fem\u003E is a rate-limiting enzyme in carotenoid synthesis and represents a precursor required for ABA synthesis in various plants (Zhou et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r72\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Zhou, Rao, Wrightstone, Sun, Lui, Welsch and Li\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2022\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOsPSY3\u003C\u002Fem\u003E has been demonstrated in previous studies using reverse transcription quantitative PCR (RT-qPCR) experiments to show upregulation of gene expression after dehydration, salt, and ABA treatment (Du et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r10\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Du, Chang, Huang and Xiong\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2015\u003C\u002Fa\u003E; Welsch et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r62\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Welsch, Wüst, Bär, Al-Babili and Beyer\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2008\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). Therefore, the selection results were consistent with those of existing studies. The identification of this gene as one of the stress-responsive genes in the previous studies provides evidence supporting the results of the meta-analysis. Other upregulated genes included transcription factor \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOsPHR3\u003C\u002Fem\u003E (\u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOs02g0139000\u003C\u002Fem\u003E). This gene is also upregulated in response to dehydration stress and confirmed by RT-qPCR in the previous study (Abdirad et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r1\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Abdirad, Ghaffari, Majd, Irian, Soleymaniniya, Daryani, Koobaz, Shobbar, Farsad, Yazdanpanah, Sadri, Mirzaei, Ghorbanzadeh, Kazemi, Hadidi, Haynes and Salekdeh\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2022\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). The expression of this gene is also induced by inorganic phosphate (Pi) deficiency and plays a role in improving tolerance to Pi deficiency as well as regulating nitrogen (N) homeostasis (Guo et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r17\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Guo, Ruan, Li, Huang, Zeng, Liu, Yu, Ding, Wu, Wu, Mao, Yi, Wu and Mo\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2015\u003C\u002Fa\u003E; Ruan et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r48\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Ruan, Guo, Wu and Yi\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2017\u003C\u002Fa\u003E; Sun et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r56\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Sun, Luo, Jain, Liu, Ai, Liu, Feng, Zhang, Zhang, Guohua and Sun\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2018\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). Deficiency of Pi or N induces various morphophysiological adaptive responses and gene expression regulation in plants (Bechtaoui et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r6\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Bechtaoui, Rabiu, Raklami, Oufdou, Hafidi and Jemo\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2021\u003C\u002Fa\u003E; Khan et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r31\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Khan, Siddique, Shabala, Zhou and Zhao\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2023\u003C\u002Fa\u003E; Sakuraba, \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r50\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Sakuraba\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2022\u003C\u002Fa\u003E; Xing et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r64\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Xing, Cao, Zhang, Wei, Zhang and Wan\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2023\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). Although several studies have suggested a relationship between Pi and N deficiency and the ABA pathway and its biosynthesis, many aspects remain unclear and further research is needed (Fang Zhu et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r13\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Fang Zhu, Sheng Zhao, Wu and Fang Shen\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2018\u003C\u002Fa\u003E; Hsieh et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r20\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Hsieh, Kan, Wu, Yang and Hsieh\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2018\u003C\u002Fa\u003E; Jaskolowski &amp; Poirier, \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r24\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Jaskolowski and Poirier\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2024\u003C\u002Fa\u003E; Zakari et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r67\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Zakari, Asad, Han, Zhao and Cheng\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2020\u003C\u002Fa\u003E; Yu Zhang et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r70\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Zhang, Li, Wang, Guo, Lu, Song, Zuo, Chen and Liu\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2022\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). The functions of these genes, specifically upregulated in resistant cultivars, suggest that they contribute to tolerance mechanisms. For example, the consistent upregulation of \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOsPSY3\u003C\u002Fem\u003E, a key enzyme in the carotenoid biosynthesis pathway that leads to the production of ABA, may enable resistant cultivars to synthesize ABA more quickly in response to stress. This could result in more efficient stomatal closure, reducing water loss and enhancing osmotic adjustment, thereby conferring drought and salt resistance. Similarly, the upregulation of \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOsPHR3\u003C\u002Fem\u003E, which regulates Pi homeostasis, could be crucial for maintaining the balance of nutrients under stress. As abiotic stresses often disrupt nutrient uptake and homeostasis, sustaining phosphate and potentially related nitrogen signaling pathways via \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOsPHR3\u003C\u002Fem\u003E could enable resistant plants to manage resources and maintain growth more effectively than susceptible ones.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E In contrast, genes specifically upregulated in susceptible cultivars included \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOsbHLH035\u003C\u002Fem\u003E (\u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOs01g0159800\u003C\u002Fem\u003E) and \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003ERRJ1\u003C\u002Fem\u003E (\u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOs10g0517500\u003C\u002Fem\u003E). A previous meta-analysis study using transcriptome data suggested that genes such as \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOsbHLH035\u003C\u002Fem\u003E and \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003ERRJ1\u003C\u002Fem\u003E were upregulated by multiple heavy metal stresses, including mercury (Hg) and lead (Pb), and were subsequently validated by RT-qPCR (Fan et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r12\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Fan, Liu, Cao, Ma, Hu, Xiang and Zhao\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2021\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). Drought-induced reductions in soil moisture can increase the concentration of heavy metals in the soil, which can have a synergistic negative effect on plants (Islam &amp; Sandhi, \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r23\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Islam and Sandhi\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2022\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). Therefore, focusing on genes such as \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOsbHLH035\u003C\u002Fem\u003E and \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003ERRJ1\u003C\u002Fem\u003E is likely to provide important clues for understanding the combined effects of heavy metal stress and drought stress and for developing resistant varieties. These genes specifically upregulated in susceptible cultivars might not signify an optimal adaptive response to salt or drought. It is plausible that their induction, potentially reflecting pathways shared with heavy metal stress, leads to suboptimal resource allocation or triggers inappropriate signaling cascades, thereby contributing to susceptibility. An alternative hypothesis is that the higher expression is merely a consequence of greater overall stress damage experienced by susceptible cultivars, resulting in a more general, less specific stress response activation that includes these genes. However, it should be noted that experimental verification of the expression of these genes under salt or drought treatment has not yet been conducted.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E Additionally, a comparison with previous \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EArabidopsis\u003C\u002Fem\u003E meta-analysis data revealed several genes whose expression was altered in \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E and \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EA. thaliana\u003C\u002Fem\u003E under both salt and drought stress conditions (\u003Ca class=\"xref table\" href=\"#tab3\"\u003ETable 3\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). To focus on genes involved in mechanisms commonly conserved between plant species regardless of the stress phenotype, we focused on genes shared by seven DEGs, with three in \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EA. thaliana\u003C\u002Fem\u003E and four in \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E. For example, \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EHSFC1\u003C\u002Fem\u003E (\u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EAT3G24520\u003C\u002Fem\u003E) represented a gene commonly upregulated in both species, regardless of phenotype.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E Previous studies on \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EA. thaliana\u003C\u002Fem\u003E have suggested that the expression of \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EHSFC1\u003C\u002Fem\u003E is involved in cold responses via a pathway independent of the C-repeat binding factor (CBF), a well-known transcription factor that controls cold acclimation in plants (Jia et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r27\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Jia, Ding, Shi, Zhang, Gong and Yang\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2016\u003C\u002Fa\u003E; Zhao et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r71\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Zhao, Zhang, Xie, Si, Li and Zhu\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2016\u003C\u002Fa\u003E).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E The ortholog of \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EArabidopsis HSFC1\u003C\u002Fem\u003E gene in \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E was \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EHSfC2b\u003C\u002Fem\u003E (\u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EOs06g0553100\u003C\u002Fem\u003E). However, the functions and roles of these genes under salinity and drought conditions remain unclear. Heat shock factors (HSFs) that contribute to environmental stress tolerance occur in both \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EA. thaliana\u003C\u002Fem\u003E and \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E (Wenjing et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r63\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Wenjing, Chen, Singh, Huang and Pei\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2020\u003C\u002Fa\u003E; Yan Zhang et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r69\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Zhang, Wang, Wang, Yun, Song, Idrees, Liu, Zhang, Yang, Zheng, Zhang and Gao\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2022\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). Given the consistent upregulation of \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EHSFC1\u003C\u002Fem\u003E and its ortholog \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EHSfC2b\u003C\u002Fem\u003E across different stress conditions and plant species, these genes are promising candidates for further investigation.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E In the cross-species comparison, the relatively limited overlap of common genes can be primarily attributed to the fact that we focused on genes shared by multiple DEG sets – specifically, three sets in \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EA. thaliana\u003C\u002Fem\u003E and four sets in \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E, totaling seven sets. Furthermore, \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E and \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EA. thaliana\u003C\u002Fem\u003E are evolutionarily highly divergent and possess distinct stress response pathways, making it natural that only a few genes exhibit similar expression changes under all conditions. Nevertheless, the genes commonly identified in both species are likely universally conserved and function as core regulatory factors in stress responses, underscoring their significant biological relevance.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E Regarding the GO term “cold acclimation” upregulated in both resistant and susceptible groups, upon examining the list of genes annotated with this term, we observed that the majority were dehydrin genes. Dehydrins contribute to drought and salt stress tolerance by being induced not only by low temperatures but also by dehydration resulting from salt and drought stresses (Hanin et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r18\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Hanin, Brini, Ebel, Toda, Takeda and Masmoudi\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2011\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). This suggests that the significant enrichment of “cold acclimation” in both resistant and susceptible groups largely reflects the activation of a common dehydration response mechanism rather than a cold-specific response.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E This study had some limitations. First, because the identification of DEGs was based on the selection of TN scores rather than statistical tests, the results should be interpreted with caution. Second, the public RNA-Seq data used in this study is an integration of data obtained under various growth conditions and experimental protocols. As a result, there are variations in stress treatment methods between experiments, and we are constrained by the necessity to rely on published metadata information for phenotype classification. The classification of resistant and susceptible phenotypes was determined primarily based on metadata. Although this practical method enabled the meta-analysis across heterogeneous datasets, it may not fully reflect the complete spectrum of stress tolerance mechanisms. These points need to be considered. Third, experimental validation using plant samples exposed to specific stress environments was not performed, indicating that further research is required to elucidate the functions of these genes. Fourth, we utilized the \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EJaponica\u003C\u002Fem\u003E reference transcriptome (IRGSP-1.0). This decision was based on several factors, including that it provides more comprehensive and continuously updated gene annotations compared to the currently available Indica reference transcriptome. This decision was based on the fact that information about each gene is easier to access for \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EJaponica\u003C\u002Fem\u003E compared to Indica. In particular, when discussing the functional interpretation of individual candidate genes identified in this meta-analysis, the information provided by Oryzabase (Kurata &amp; Yamazaki, \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r32\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Kurata and Yamazaki\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2006\u003C\u002Fa\u003E) and RAP-DB (Sakai et al., \u003Ca class=\"xref bibr\" href=\"#r49\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"show-for-sr\"\u003EReference Sakai, Lee, Tanaka, Numa, Kim, Kawahara, Wakimoto, Yang, Iwamoto, Abe, Yamada, Muto, Inokuchi, Ikemura, Matsumoto, Sasaki and Itoh\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E2013\u003C\u002Fa\u003E), which are major databases providing access to functional information and research papers on rice genes, is much more extensive for \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EJaponica\u003C\u002Fem\u003E than for Indica. A key point here is that the TN ratio, the primary analytical metric in this study, is calculated within each experimental project as the ratio of gene expression levels (TPM) between paired stressed and control samples. This means that for datasets of Indica cultivars, the expression ratio is calculated between Indica stressed samples and Indica control samples. Therefore, we are not directly comparing absolute expression values between \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EJaponica\u003C\u002Fem\u003E and Indica across studies or cultivars, but rather focusing on the relative expression changes during stress response within each experiment. Consequently, even if a mismatch between our \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EJaponica\u003C\u002Fem\u003E reference sequence and Indica samples affects absolute TPM values, as long as both treated and control groups are similarly affected, the impact on their ratio, i.e., the TN ratio, is considered to be relatively small. Furthermore, the TN score method is a system that assigns higher scores to genes whose expression changes are consistently observed across a large number of datasets. In relation to the use of this \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EJaponica\u003C\u002Fem\u003E reference, when comparing mapping to the Indica reference available on Ensembl Plants and the \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EJaponica\u003C\u002Fem\u003E reference (IRGSP-1.0), 102 out of the 110 Indica samples used in this study indeed showed higher mapping rates to the \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EJaponica\u003C\u002Fem\u003E reference (Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003ETable S21\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). While this suggests a certain validity in selecting the \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EJaponica\u003C\u002Fem\u003E reference, it is still possible that mapping efficiency could be reduced in some samples due to reference sequence mismatch. However, in the TN score method, even if mapping efficiency is low for some samples, if consistent expression changes are not detected in many other pairs, the specific variation in that sample is, in principle, unlikely to significantly impact the overall conclusions. In fact, for the drought-resistant category, when comparing the results from analyses excluding 2 pairs, 4 samples with low mapping rates (SRR11342745, SRR11342746, SRR11342749, SRR11342750) from its total of 31 paired datasets, versus using all samples for this category, over 95% of the DEGs were common (Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003ETable S22a\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003EFigure S8a\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). Additionally, this study mainly used samples of leaves and shoots, with relatively few samples derived from roots. Therefore, due to the principle of TN score calculation, expression patterns specific to tissues with fewer samples, such as roots in this study, tend to have a relatively lower contribution to the overall score. We also compared the analysis results for the salt susceptible category when its root samples were excluded versus when all its tissues were used (Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003ETable S22b\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003Ec\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003Ed\u003C\u002Fa\u003E)). For this salt susceptible category, when comparing the DEG results from the analysis excluding its 6 pairs of root samples (from its total of 36 paired datasets) with the analysis using all tissues for this category, approximately 70% of the genes were common. Enrichment analysis of these common genes for the salt-susceptible category confirmed that similar terms were enriched as in the analysis using all tissues for this category (Supplementary \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003EFigure S8b\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003E8c\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.6084\u002Fm9.figshare.25547083.v4\"\u003E8d\u003C\u002Fa\u003E)). However, the genes identified in this study are likely to reflect changes predominantly observed in leaves and shoots, which are the majority in our analyzed datasets, or changes common across tissue types. These limitations should be considered when interpreting our results and planning future studies.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003Cdiv class=\"sec conclusions\" data-magellan-destination=\"sec20\" id=\"sec20\"\u003E\u003Ch2 class=\"A\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label\"\u003E5.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E Conclusion\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E Through a meta-analysis of publicly available RNA-Seq data, we obtained a list of potential target genes related to drought and salt stress responses in \u003Cem class=\"italic\"\u003EO. sativa\u003C\u002Fem\u003E and identified candidate genes that may influence stress-related phenotypes. These findings provide a valuable resource for future studies aimed at understanding the molecular mechanisms underlying stress resistance in rice and developing new strategies to improve crop productivity under adverse environmental conditions.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003Cdiv class=\"back\"\u003E\n\u003Cdiv class=\"sec\" data-magellan-destination=\"sec21\" id=\"sec21\"\u003E\u003Ch2 class=\"A\"\u003E Open peer review\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp class=\"p\"\u003E To view the open peer review materials for this article, please visit \u003Ca class=\"uri\" href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.1017\u002Fqpb.2025.10020\"\u003Ehttp:\u002F\u002Fdoi.org\u002F10.1017\u002Fqpb.2025.10020\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003Cdiv Center.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003Cdiv class=\"sec coi-statement\" data-magellan-destination=\"sec22\" id=\"sec22\"\u003E\u003Ch2 class=\"A\"\u003E Competing
