class=\"article-title\"\u003EAuthor comment: Meta-analysis of public RNA-sequencing data of drought and salt stresses in different phenotypes of resistant and susceptible \u003Cspan class=\"italic\"\u003EOryzasativa\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E cultivars — R0\u002FPR1\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E",productId:"1105AFD3ACD6E7FCB2A07821D9152272",position:k,sections:[],contributor:{givenNames:B,surname:C,nameStyle:e,affiliations:[{text:af}],isCorresponding:a,notes:e,isAnonymous:a,fullName:D,searchUrl:E,orcidUrl:F},comments:"\u003Cp\u003EOctober 17, 2024\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EDr. Oliver Hamant,\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EEditor in Chief\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EQuantitative Plant Biology\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EDear Editor:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EI wish to submit an article titled “Meta-analysis of public RNA-sequencing data of drought and salt stresses in different phenotypes of \u003Cspan class=\"italic\"\u003EOryza sativa\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E” for publication in \u003Cspan class=\"italic\"\u003EQuantitative Plant Biology\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E. The paper was coauthored by Mitsuo Shintani.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003ESalinity and drought are major abiotic stresses that inhibit plant growth and productivity. Rice is susceptible to the negative effects of drought and salt damage, which lead to serious issues of reduced yields. In this study, we collected RNA sequencing (RNA-Seq) data from \u003Cspan class=\"italic\"\u003EOryza sativa subsp. indica\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E and \u003Cspan class=\"italic\"\u003EOryza sativa subsp. japonica\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E registered in public databases and conducted a meta-analysis integrating multiple studies. Focusing on two types of stress conditions (salt and drought), we aimed to identify novel stress-responsive genes in \u003Cspan class=\"italic\"\u003EOryza sativa\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E by comparing RNA-Seq data from stress-resistant and stress-susceptible cultivars. We analyzed 105 paired datasets with different phenotypes under drought and salt stress conditions to identify genes with common expression changes across multiple studies. Meta-analysis identified 10 genes specifically upregulated in resistant cultivars and 12 specifically upregulated in susceptible cultivars under both drought and salt stress conditions. Furthermore, by comparing previously identified stress-responsive genes in \u003Cspan class=\"italic\"\u003EArabidopsis thaliana\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E, we explored genes potentially involved in stress response mechanisms that are conserved across plant species. We believe that our study makes a significant contribution to the literature because our study obtained a list of potential target genes related to drought and salt stress responses in \u003Cspan class=\"italic\"\u003EOryza sativa\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E and identified candidate genes that may influence stress-related phenotypes. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EFurther, we believe that this paper will be of interest to the readership of \u003Cspan class=\"italic\"\u003EQuantitative Plant Biology\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E because the findings of this study provide a new perspective for basic research on the stress response mechanisms in rice. Moreover, the identified genes have the potential for use as target candidates for genome editing to develop stress-resistant rice.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWe confirm that neither the manuscript nor any parts of its content are currently under consideration for publication with or published in another journal. While the authors have taken the impact of instrumentation and other factors into account in their data selection criteria, they need to address two key points more thoroughly.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EFirstly, as noted by Reviewer 1, the influence of the potential mapping biases due to sequence variations between japonica and indica should not be overlooked. Although differences in gene presence\u002Fabsence or sequence variations among subspecies are possible, it is essential to demonstrate that the observed differences in the candidate genes identified in this study are due to expression differences, rather than variations in genomic structure.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003ESecondly, while the authors have utilized the reference genome from the Ensemble Plants, more recent reference genomes are available in databases such as Gramene (https:\u002F\u002Foryza-ensembl.gramene.org\u002Findex.html). Additionally, Supplementary TableS2 indicates that the authors have used data from various tissues, including leaf and root, in their analysis.
